(рейрен-реорел) рек. рддрдВрежрдЖреж (резредрезрел) рел. рддрдВрежрдЖреж (резредрейрейреж) рем. рддрдВреж рдЖреж (резрезреиреорек-реиреорел, реорезрел) рен. рдпрдЪрд╛рд╕реНрддрд┐ рднреЛрдЧреЛ рди рдЪ рддрддреНрд░ рдореЛрдХреНрд╖реЛ ред рдпрддреНрд░рд╛рд╕реНрддрд┐ рдореЛрдХреНрд╖реЛ рди рдЪ рддрддреНрд░ рднреЛрдЧрдГ ред рд╢реНрд░реАрд╕реБрдиреНрджрд░реА рд╕реЗрд╡рдирддрддреНрдкрд░рд╛рдгрд╛рдВ рднреЛрдЧрд╢реНрдЪрдореЛрдХреНрд╖рд╢реНрдЪ рдХрд░рд╕реНрде рдПрд╡ редред Indroduction (1) Veda and Tantra India is a country of unity full of diversity. From distant past the current of physical and spiritual knowledge has been flowing on this earth. Vedas, Upani┼Яads, Pur─Бс╣Зas and other physical and spiritual scriptures have been running in the stream of study and teaching. Philosophy is a venerable canal of this stream. The summumbonum of all knowledge is freedom from all sufferings. The treatises other than those of philosophy, guide to a way of freedom which is impermanent dincomplete. Philosophy is The only highway which leads to permanent and complete salvation. Between the two Philosophies viz Indian and Western, the latter talks of theory only, its practical side is zero. There are two main streams of Indian philosophy Vaidika and Agamika. The Ganga Yamun─Б of theory and practice flow simultaneously in these streams. In the root of Vaidika Sadhan─Б there are Vedas where as in the root of Tantrika s─Бdhan─Б there are Tantras. In their beginning these two streams were flowing in their pure perspective but later on they become intermixed. Not only this, there happened submixing in other disciplines also and as a result of this the Vaidika and T─Бntrika schools became complementary to each other and the T─Бntrika scholars had to declare тАФ ‘Right from Garbh─Бdh─Бna (impregnation) to marriage one should adopt Vaidika way, later on he sould follow T─Бntrika or ┼Ъaiva tradition. Introduction 37 Although Vedas and Tantra are visible in the form of words, they are two phases of one knowledge. This knowledge is devine and nonhuman. Apparently what so ever meaning be understood of Veda, really this means a particular knowledge which is devine subtle beyond the congizance of senses. Having gotten this particular knowledge the seers of mantras, the r╚Щis used to be omniscient and in the last having selfrealization they reached the culmination of life i.e. liberation. In Pur─Бkalpa it is said тАФ “The rsis were the seers of mantras the visualisers of Dharma. They had vision of subtle eternal nonsensuous V─Бk (sound, Speech). This speech was delivered to those who had not vision of this, just like events realized in dream. The preachings of them are in the form of Veda and Ved─Б├▒ga. Having taken the help of gross scheech they expressed the unspeakable and that is Veda. Really and originally the Veda is one. This is not speech but realization. At the time of mnifestation it takes the fom of speech and manifests itself in word-sequence. Veda is the means of Brahma-realization. This realization comes after the demolish of l-knot . This I-knot shines in the form of ‘I’ and ‘My’. The present form of vedas is seen in many forms. These are imitation of that realization which is partless and unspeakable. Yogi bhart─Ыhari says ‘Although the Veda is one yet this is told by great r╚Щis in many ways which is imitation and means of achievement of that (unspeakable V─Бk).’ Just like Veda the Tantra is also the object of realization and speech. The Sakti (potency or power) inherent in Siva has two forms viz. j├▒─Бna (knowledge) and Kriy─Б (action). The j├▒─Бna is of two kindsтАФ Para (Superior) and Apara (non-superior), the para j├▒─Бna is bodh─Бtmaka (apprehensible) while Apara J├▒─Бna is V─Бg─Б╚Ыmaka (speakable). This speakable knowledge is set up in the form of ┼а─Бstra (scripture). The apprehensible knowledge becomes capable to express its meaning only when it takes the help of speakable knowledge. In the very beginning of creation 38 Tantraloka lord Parama S─лva manifests the knowledge for salvation of individual selves. This menifested Knowledge, when takes the form of speech, gets the name of ‘Tantra’. Tantra : Form and Scope The other name (Synonim) of Tantra is Agama. The coustituent alphalets of the word ─Аgama i.e. ─А, ga and ma denote three facts which are incorporated in the verse ─Аgatam s─лiva Vakrtebhyo gatam ca Girij─Б ┼Ъrutau. Matam ca V─Бsudeven tasmad─Бgama ucyate. This meaning of the verse is thatтАФThe Agamas are scriptures come out of the mouths of Siva. These were told to P─Бrvat─л. V─Бsudeva, K─Бrt─лkeya, Garuna etc. have given their consent to them. This Agama is known by the name of Tantra. The word Tantra denotes expansion. The root is, ‘Tanu’ and the suffix is ‘Tral’ or ‘stran’ Thus the word “Tantra’ indicates expansion. This expansion is of soul. Parama ┼Ъ─лva due to His freedom diminishes Himself and manifests in the form of concious and enert things at his own accordance. Later on by several means he sets aside his diminution and having expanded or made himself perfect, He rests in His own self. The procedure of Parama Siva’s menifestation in the form of universe and then return in His own self is the subject-matter of Tantra. Tantra is a pattern of self-realization. It is a highway, an art, a scientific method which leads to self-realization, to perfect I-ness very quickly. Although Tantra is an independent subject yet it is middle point. Before Tantra there is Mantra and after there is Yantra. Amongst these three points one remains incomplete without the rest two. To know the fundamentals of the things is Mantra. To know the possible conditions by the conjugation and mixture of things and then to give it a form, is called Tantra. To mark or to point out this conjugation and mixture by figures, letters and lines is called Yantra. There is an entity which is uncognigible, partless, undivided unspeakable. Introduction 39 It is called Parama. When this entity assumes the state of knowledge by his sovereignty it becomes Mantra, and then the word, which is an assembly of letters, plays important role. When the aforesaid knowledge takes the form of action it becomes Tantra. By the Japa of Mantra the corpuscles of body develop and then by the strength achieved through this development, the practiser (=s─Бdhaka) pierces the Cakras. This process of piercing of Cakras is suggested by Yantra. There are two objectives of Tantra - worldly and transcen dental. To know the natural phenomenon as well as that unspeakable entity which is beyond this nature, by the help of expansion, and then by unveiling the mysterious nature to make it useful for human being, is the worldly motto of Tantra. Having known the expansion to know the root of this (expansion) is the transcendental object of Tantra. The latter which means to rest in its own self is the summumbonum of Tantra. The Vedas teach aversion, therefore they can lead to salvation only, although Dharma, Artha and K─Бma (Virtue, money and sex) also are their objects but they are of secondary importance. Since the salvation does not happen in group therefore the Vedas, treat with individual. Tantra has both objectives worldly enjoyment and salvation. By worldly attach ment it does good to individual and society both. Through this it leads to realization of oneness and makes identification with the whole of the universe. This is its ultimate aim or goal. Tantra is a method of investigation. Science also investigates but it investigates the outer things by outer instruments. The field of scientific research is external world. There is an internal world also and it is as vast as the external one. Tantra explores this internal world. Scientific research pertains to inert things where as Tantrika research aims at concious one which is alpervasive and is known by the words “Tat’, ‘Brahma’, ‘Parama Siva’, ‘Param─Б Sakti’ etc. There are two concious entities cognized in the worldтАФ Tat (That i.e. ultimate Self) and ‘Aham’ (I’ i.e. individual self). Apparently and 40 Tantraloka philologically both are different. One is third person the other is first person. The third person is alperfect while the first person is imperfect, but really and ultimately both are one and same. The ‘Tat’ manifests in the form of ‘Aham’. The history of manifestations of ‘Tat’ in the form of ‘Aham’ and the procedure of identification or assimilation of ‘Aham’ with “Tat’ is the subject matter of Tantra. The nasal or zero of Sanskrit alphabets ( o ) is the symbol of ultimate reality or big vacuum (= mah─Б┼Ы┼лnya) of Tantra. When two zeros unite ‘it becomes visarga (: 8) i.e. creation. It means that when big vacuum i.e. ┼Ъiva seperates Him from Himself within Himself there happens visarga or creation. This visarga is the symbol of the coupling state of ┼Ъiva and ┼Ъakti. Three zeros make a triangleтАФThere are two types of triangles with upward edge A and with downword edge V. The first triangle symbolizes Siva and second one symbolizes ┼Ъakti. When these two types of triangles are conjugated a hexangle is made. This hexangle symbolizes eternal relation or conjugation of Siva and Sakti. All the men and women of the world symbolize ┼Ъiva and Sakti. Further each and every body is partially a synthesis of Siva and Sakti. In the body marrow, semen, Vital air and soul represent ┼Ъ─лva while bone, skin , blood, flesh and fat represent Sakti. These nine elements in the body are suggested by nine angles fo ┼Ъr─лcakra. According to law of Pinda-Brahm─Бnda (i.e. just as in individual body same in universe), the same condition is in the universe also. M─Бy─Б, Suddhavidy─Б, Iswara and Sad─Бs─лva represent ┼Ъ─лva. Where as mah─Бbh┼лta represent ┼Ъakti. The figure of ┼Ъr─лcakra presents equality of Pinda and Brahm─Бnda. Tantra introduces this equality in all dimensions well. S─Бdhka (i.e. Practiser of Tantra) pierces the cover of elements, unviels them and then crosses the stages of Bindu, Ardhacandra, Rodhin─л, N─Бda, N─Бd─Бnta, ┼Ъakti, Vy─Бpin─л and saman─Б, step by step ultimately he reaches Unman─Б where the difference of ‘Tat’ and ‘Aham’ Vanishes and S─Бdhaka achieves Introduction 41 identity with ┼Ъiva. This is the subject matter which is dealt with Tantra. There are three kinds of the scripure told by Siva-Agama, Yamala and Tantra. ─Аgama deals with creation annihilation, god-worship. practice of Mantra, Purascaraс╣Зa, meditaion, six acts (i.e. killing, fascination, expulsion, enmity, attraction and subjugation). The topic of Y─Бmala is creation. astrology, Spiritual routine work, S┼лtra, creed, caste, ethics. The subject matter and scope of Tantra is very vast. Along with physical world and spiritual infinity it includes the whole of the topics related to Agama and Y─Бmala.   1. TraditionalтАФAccording to tradition and faith Tantra is beginningless or eternal. They had the way of salvation. When Kaliyuga commenced on and those traditional systems became rare and confined specially to Kalapi Villege, Lord Siva in the form of Sr─лkantha wandering on the mountain Kail─Бsa ordered sage Durv─Б┼Ы─Б to proclaim it lest it should come to an end.”

Assam and Bengal were main centres of T─Бntrika practices in those days. From there Tantra was taken to other Indian states or foreign countries. Tantra Litertature-Middle Age The medieval period of Tantrika literature can be fixed from the 1st century A.D. to the 10th centrury A.D. In this age texts were written pertainning to the worships of different dieties. These texts were based on old T─Бntrika literature. It is not irrelevant to say that in this period ┼Ъ─Бkta worship was prevalent in big proportion. As a result most of the texts were written related to S─Бkta-worship. Ac─Бrya Abhinavagupta was the topmost scholar of saiva tradition in this period. Besides the Tantr─Бloka he wrote a number of books of different disciplines. Ksemar─Бja, (pratyabhij├▒─Бhrdya etc.), Jaiyaratha (Tantr─Бlokaviveka ‘K─Бmakal─Бvil─Б┼Ыa), Yogar─Бja, ┼Ъivop─Бdhy─Бya, Maheswar─Бnanda (Mah─Бrthama├▒jar─л), Sr─лvatsa (Cidgagana candrik─Б) Siti kantha (Mah─Бnayaprak─Б┼Ыa), Pusy─Бnandan─Бtha, Swatantr─Бnandan─Бtha (M─Бtrk─Бcakra viveka), V─Бt┼лlan─Бtha (s┼лtra), cakrap─Б┼Жin─Бtha, (Bh─Бvopah─Бra), Vir┼лp─Бk┼Яan─Бtha (Vir┼л paksapa├▒c─Б┼Ыik─Б) etc. were other scholars who by writing original texts and commentaries made the ┼Ъaiva Sastra prosperous. Among the western scholars of Tantra the names of Sir John Woodruff (the serpent power etc.) and Arthur Avalon can be taken with respect. Mah─Бmaho-p─Бdhy─Бya Harapras─Бda sastr─л, Prabodha candra B─Бgac─л, Krsn─Бnanda Agama V─Бg─Б┼Ыa (Tantras─Бra), Tripur─Бnanda, Brahm─Бnanda giri, P┼лrn─Бnandan─Бtha (Sy─Бm─Бrahasya) Purn─Бnanda paramahamsa parivr─Бjaka (s─Бktakrama, ┼Ъr─лtatwacint─Бmani etc.), ┼аamkara ─Бgam─Бc─Бrya (T─Бr─Бrahasyavsttik─Б), Narsimhath─Бkura (T─Бr─Б bhaktisudh─Бrnava), Kr┼Яnamohana (Agamacandr─лk─Б), Candra sekhara (Purascary─Б d─лpik─Б, Kulap┼лj─Бcandrik─Б), R─Бma gop─Бlasarm─Б (Tantrad─лpan─л), K─Б┼б─лn─Бtha tark─Бlamk─Бra (Sy─Бm─Б sapary─Бvidhi), J├▒─Бn─Бnanda brahmc─Бr─л (Tatwa prak─Б┼Ыa), R─Бdh─Бmohana (T─лksn─Б Kalpa) etc. were the authors of Tantrika texts. These were inhabitants of Beng─Бla and flowrished between 11th to 16th centuries. In Mah─Бr─Б┼Ыtra N─лlakantha was a ┼Ъaiva scholar who wrote a number of books. Introduction 59 [2] K─Б┼Ыm─лra ┼Ъaiva (Tantra) Dar┼Ыana IntroductionтАФThe current of indian knowledge and practice (s─Бdhan─Б) has been flowing in two ways viz. Nigama and Agama. If the source of Vaidika knowedge is the exhalation of Vi┼Яnu the source of Tantra is the mouth of ┼а─лva. To speak the truth both these two systems are beginningless and independent. As per the nature of human being the followers of these two systems became influenced by each other and a partial mixing of principle and practice happened on both sides. The result was that a mixed discipline came into practice. In the Vaidika literature Rudras┼лkta, as well as some Upanisats like. ┼Ъwet─Б┼Ъwatara, P─Б┼Ыupata, Brahma, Tripur─Бt─Бpin─л, Tripura, Katharudra, Bh─Бvan─Б etc., are proofs of tantric mixing in Vaidika literature. Similarly in tantrika worships and rituals the use of Vaidika mantras prove that Tantra was influenced by Vaidika system. Even then there are some fundamental doctrines of Tantra which discriminate and particularize it from Veda.
  19. Ultimate Reality - All the philosophies of the east and the west are of the opinion that there is a concious being where from this universe comes off. Tantra is not an exception to it. the entity which has been accepted here is partless. The most profound state of the perfect entity is beyond imagination of Sat, Cit and Ananda. It is a complete whole and without distinction. In this perfound and pure being an offshoot (Kal─Б) come out. This is self-luminous. In T─Бntrika word it is called Cit or Citi. This Citi (concious-ness is the first ray of self manifestion of that ultimate entiry. According to T─Бntr─лka term nology it is called Anuttara (the last). The first vowel of Samskrta language or the first alphabet of M─Бheswara s┼лtra ‘a’ symbolizes this ‘Anuttara’. This concious 60 Tantraloka Kala always flows from the ultimate reality. Just as due to Spandana (throbbing) the ‘Cit’ manifests in ‘Sat’ similary in ‘Cit’ also throbbing happens continuously. As a result of this throbbing the ‘Cit’ countinues its association with ‘Sat’ on one hand and on the other, another ‘Cit’ appears in previous ‘Cit’. When the second Cit reflects in the first ‘Cit’ the former realizes its appearance. This recognition of its own entity is called ‘Ananda’. Just as we look our face in the mirror and feel pleassure, the same condition is there. By the above statement it is proved that the partless (akhanda) entity is concious. ‘Sat’ and ‘Cit’ are one and same. This entity is independent i.e. selfsustained having no assistance from anywhere. By ‘Satyam’, ‘Sivam’, ‘Sunderam’ or by Sat, Cit, Ananda this very entity is suggested. From viewpoint of manifestation this entity is Cit and from viewpoint of sentiment (Ras─Бsv─Бda) it is Ananda. According to saivites it is Paramasiva, and according to ┼Ъakt─Бs it is Param─Б┼Ъakti. P┼лrva kaulas say that there is sesa, Sesi bh─Бva (relation of part and whole) between them. Uttara Kaulas do not accept it. The reality is that there is not any type of relation between the two. They are not dicotomous but identical. Following Gajavrsabha ny─Бya. it is Paramas─лva as well as Param─Б Sakti. Without Sakti s─лva devoid of Iccha j├▒ana and Kriy─Б, is just like Sava (corps), incapable to throb. This fact is indicated in the first worse of Saundaryalahar─л.? In absence of concious ┼Ъ─лva, Sakti can not be capable to mamifest her. Just as fire and its burning power are identical in the same way ┼Ъ─лva and ┼Ъakti are one and same. This state is of ultimate
  20. A picture if looked from one side seems to be of elephant where as looked from other side it seem to be of bull. This is called Gajavrsabha ny─Бya (maxim of elephant and bull) 2. Sivah sakty─Б yukto yadi bhavati saktah prabhavitum. na cedevam devah na khalu saktah spanditumapi. Introduction 61 equilibrium and non-duality. There is no discrimination of gender. Although this state is of non-duality yet if we think from dualistic point of view both ┼Ъiva and Sakti are difference. From worldly point of view Siva is motionless as well as witness while ┼Ъakti does five acts (Pancakrtya) continuously. This perfect ultimate reality is both immanent and transendent simultaneously. On one hand this is ┼Ъiva which is completely ┼Ъ┼лnya (Zero, vaccuum) at the same time on the other hand it is s─Бkti i.e. the whole the perfect the complete the immanent universe, meaning there by that the union of Parama Siva and Param─Б ┼Ы─Бkt─л is eternal. The thought of ardhan─Бr─л┼Ыwara (god ┼Ъiva having his body half of male and half of female) expresses the same idea. Here Siva and Sakti are eternally present and this is why to a Siddhayogi this world seems to be identical because there is nothing other that the playful Mah─Б Sakti.
  21. Sw─Бtantrya-Doctrine of swatantrya is the life breath of agama. The supreme entity parama Siva is supreme free. Due to this nature. He always keeps Himself embelished with five ┼Ъaktis viz Cit, Ananda, Icch─Б, J├▒ana and Kriy─Б (= conciousness, bliss, desire, knowledge and activity); Sat He is Himself. Cit is inner-potency. Aananda is His outer strength. The Kaul─Бc─Бryas think Him immanent The Tantra c─Бryas take him to be transcendent. But the Trika school or K─Б┼Ыm─лra ┼Ъaiva philosohpy says that the supreme entity is both immanent and transcendent simulteanously. This is due to His sw─Бtantrya. The whole of the universe is a drama of his sw─Бtantrya. Due to this sw─Бtantrya He has composed the drama of the world. He Himself is dramatizing it in different forms and at the same time He is seeing this drama played by Him as spectator and relishing. Simultaneously He is resting in His ownself. Doing all He is doing nothing and doing nothing He is the only doer of all. He is the supreme enjoyment (param bhoga) and 62 Tantraloka ultimate renunciation (paramaty─Бga) and at the same time He is beyond enjoyment and renunciation. Everywhere He is self luminous, omnipresent still He is not availed even after inner and outer search. Adorned with unlimited glory, He is Brahma of j├▒─Бnins (enlightened ones), Param─Бtm─Б of yogins and God (Bhagaw─Бna) of devotees. Being insentient unspeakable and uncognizible. He is allsentient allspeakble and allcongnizible. He is Sat as well as self luminous i.e. Cit or concious. He is aware of His conciousness. This awareness of conciousness is called ‘Vimar┼Ыa’. When He becomes aware of His selfl uminosity He bocomes over joyed. His conciousness and awareness is eternal. This awareness is His sw─Бtantrya. Due to this sw─Бtantrya He is always aware of His entity and omnipotency. This universe also is the result of His awareness. This uviverse eternally rests in the ultimate entity and the awareness of this universe continues in Him. Due to this awareness He is always engazed in five acts viz. creation, preservation, destruction concealment and liberation. His own desire to conceal Him within Himself is called ’nigraha’. After creation, preservation and destruction of the universe when He comes back to His own fundamental Self then this state is called ‘anugraha’. These five acts continue in Him perpetually due to His swatantrya. There is not any reason or motto behind these acts. This is simply his swatantrya and playfulness. Due to this playfulness He takes the shape of individual self (anu). Five acts is His nature because He is omnipotent. Just as playfulness is His nature in the same way to be beyond this playfulness also is His nature. All this is grandeur of His sw─Бtantrya. 4. Pratibimba aur ─Бbh─Бsa (Reflection and appearance) The doctrine of reflection is indicated in the first two s┼лtras of the Pratyabhij├▒─Бhrdayam!. In common worldly behaviour
  22. Citih swatantr─Б Vi┼Ыwasiddhihetuh (Pr. h. 5.1.) S─Б swecchay─Б swabhittau vi┼Ыwamunm─лlayati (Pr. 4.5.2) Introduction 63 there is a bimba (figure or thing) e.g. face and the other is pratibimba (reflection) e.g. shadow in the mirror. There can be no reflection without figure like face and without base like mirror. The ulitimate reality is one and nondual. Therefore it reflects itself in its own entity due to its swatantrya. It has been told above that the first throbbing in unlimited ‘Sat’ is called ‘Cit’ the second ‘Cit’ born off the first ‘Cit’ when looks its own self in the first ‘Cit’ and becomes exhilarated, this is reflection. In practical life too we become overjoyed when we observe our reflection in some concious agent say for, wife or children or some inert things like, painting, picture, natural scence etc. This whole universe full of inumerable strangeness if seen from the point of view of creation is the refection of that ultimate reality. Just as reflection is nothing other than the base e.g. mirror etc. similarly this universe is nothing other than the ultimate reality. Just as we become aware of our reflection in the mirror similarly that ultimate reality is always aware of the universe created by and reflected in It. This awareness is appearance (─Бbh─Бsa). Just as people are aware of the waves, whirls, bubbles born in ocean etc. likewise this limitless universe which is reflected in its ownself, is always known to it. This function of awareness of unlimited strangeness also is the playfulness of it. If our mind is inclined somewhere other than the mirror, we can not rather do not be aware of our reflecton. This is not the case with the ultimate reality. It is always aware of its reflections in it. Therefore just as ultimate entity is eternal in the same way its reflections and appearances also are eternal. Literature of K─Б┼бm─лra ┼Ъaiva-Tantra Saiv─л s─Бdhana is beginningless.
